# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# HTTP Health Check Endpoint Conventions Across Go Projects

## Your Task

Find and compare how /healthz and /readyz endpoints are implemented across kubernetes/kubernetes, grafana/grafana, and prometheus/prometheus. Identify the Go source files in each repo that register these endpoints and what checks each performs (DB, cache, dependencies).

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

  ],

  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

81-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis document at `/workspace/answer.json` that details how health check endpoints are implemented across the three repositories.

## Summary

**Kubernetes (kubernetes/kubernetes):**
- Uses `/healthz`, `/livez`, and `/readyz` endpoints
- Implements a sophisticated registry-based health check system in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz/`
- Includes built-in checks: PingHealthz, LogHealthz, InformerSyncHealthz, ShutdownHealthz
- Supports etcd connectivity checks via `etcd-readiness` grouped checks
- Allows excluding checks via query parameters

**Grafana (grafana/grafana):**
- `/healthz`: Simple endpoint that returns 200 OK if running
- `/api/health`: Comprehensive endpoint with database health checks
- Database check via `SELECT 1` query with 5-second caching
- Also proxies `/livez`, `/readyz` endpoints to API server

**Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus):**
- Uses `/-/healthy` (always succeeds) and `/-/ready` (conditional on ready status)
- Implements `ReadyStatus` enum with NotReady/Ready/Stopping states
- Uses `testReady()` wrapper to conditionally serve traffic
- Includes `X-Prometheus-Stopping` header for graceful shutdown indication
- Wraps critical endpoints like `/federate` with readiness checks

The document includes all relevant source files, key symbols/functions, call chains, and detailed explanations of each implementation's approach to health checking and dependency verification.

Future changes will allow this to vary by group\n84: \t// version (for when the inevitable meta/v2 group emerges).\n85: \tMetaGroupVersion *schema.GroupVersion\n86: \n87: \t// Scheme includes all of the types used by this group and how to convert between them (or\n88: \t// to convert objects from outside of this group that are accepted in this API).\n89: \t// TODO: replace with interfaces\n90: \tScheme *runtime.Scheme\n91: \t// NegotiatedSerializer controls how this group encodes and decodes data\n92: \tNegotiatedSerializer runtime.NegotiatedSerializer\n93: \t// ParameterCodec performs conversions for query parameters passed to API calls\n94: \tParameterCodec runtime.ParameterCodec\n95: \n96: \t// StaticOpenAPISpec is the spec derived from the definitions of all resources installed together.\n97: \t// It is set during InstallAPIGroups, InstallAPIGroup, and InstallLegacyAPIGroup.\n98: \tStaticOpenAPISpec map[string]*spec.Schema\n99: }\n100: \n101: ",
